{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01NUMNXmh8Nn1P9keE7gNEE4","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I can see that `MemoryRecords.writeTo()` reads from the `buffer` directly at `position`. If this buffer has been cleared and reused by `BufferPool.deallocate()`, the data being read during the network write would be corrupted.\n\nLet me understand more clearly. The `buffer` in `MemoryRecords` is the same ByteBuffer that is pooled. When the batch is \"deallocated\" via `BufferPool.deallocate()`:\n```java\npublic void deallocate(ByteBuffer buffer, int size) {\n    lock.lock();\n    try {\n\n\n```\n\nClearing the buffer...\n\nThe `buffer.clear()` call resets the position and limit but doesn't zero out the data, so it remains until overwritten. The real problem emerges when a new batch gets allocated from the pool and starts writing to this same buffer—if the old batch's network write is still in flight, the data gets corrupted mid-transmission.\n\nLet me trace through the exact race condition: First, a produce request for batch B1 gets queued and starts writing to the network, but the socket buffer fills up partway through. Meanwhile, the `NetworkSend` object holds a reference to B1's `MemoryRecords`. Then in the next iteration, B1 gets marked as expired and the buffer gets recycled back to the pool, where a new batch immediately starts overwriting it while B1's network write is still incomplete. The issue is that the ProduceRequest header gets serialized with topic A's name, but the ByteBuffer containing the actual records has been reused and now holds topic B's data. Since the CRC checksum only covers the record payload and not the request header's topic metadata, the broker accepts the request as valid but stores topic B's records under topic A's partition—the mismatch goes undetected. WRONG direction from what the bug description says. The description says \"messages published to topic A occasionally appear on topic B instead\". Then when step 3 occurs, the network write reads the now-corrupted buffer.\n\nBut wait - the user thread writes to the buffer to append records, and then when the Sender thread calls `client.poll()`, it would write the wrong data. But the ProduceRequest for the expired batch was never sent (it was failed before being sent), so there's no pending NetworkSend for the expired batch.\n\nLet me think through the actual race condition more carefully. If a batch expires mid-flight while the network is still writing its data, the Sender thread deallocates the buffer. But a user thread could immediately reuse that same buffer for a new batch. When the network layer continues writing the original batch's data, it's now writing from a corrupted buffer that contains the new batch's records instead.\n\nThe vulnerability is in the ordering: `failBatch()` deallocates before the network write completes, and there's no synchronization preventing buffer reuse. Batch()` at line 835 — calls `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch`\n3. `Sender.java`: `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` at line 172-175 — calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)`\n4. `RecordAccumulator.java`: `deallocate()` at line 1027-1033 — calls `free.deallocate(batch.buffer()...)`\n5. `BufferPool.java`: `deallocate()` at line 260-275 — clears and returns buffer to free pool\n6. `MemoryRecords.java`: `writeTo()` at line 68-75 — reads from the buffer during network write\n\nThe root cause is that `failBatch` deallocates the buffer while a previous iteration's network write for that same batch might still be in flight through the Selector's send queue. When `sendProducerData` runs, it fails expired batches and deallocates their buffers, but `client.poll()` hasn't finished flushing those pending network sends yet, so the MemoryRecords object is still trying to read from a buffer that's been returned to the pool. The buffer gets reused for a new batch while the network send is still pending, so the broker receives topic B's data with topic A's headers. The solution is either to hold the buffer until the network write completes, or to copy the data into a separate buffer so the original can be freed immediately. Looking at how the Kafka Selector works, once data is written to the kernel socket buffer, the ByteBuffer should be safe to reuse—but the problem occurs specifically when the socket buffer fills up and the write only partially completes.\n\nWhen that happens, the `NetworkSend` still has unwritten data in the ByteBuffer, and the next `poll()` call will try to continue writing from where it left off. If the batch deallocates and reuses that buffer in the meantime, the next write will send corrupted data. The fix is to keep the batch's buffer alive until the `NetworkSend` finishes completely, which means not deallocating in-flight batches until their network writes are confirmed done.\n\nLooking at the code path in `sendProducerData()`...\n\nTracing through the logic...\n\nthe expired in-flight batches are from previous iterations, while the freshly drained `batches` variable hasn't been sent yet, so they shouldn't overlap. The real problem emerges when a batch gets marked as expired while its network write is still in progress—the batch was sent in an earlier cycle, queued in the client, but only partially written to the socket before the expiry check runs.\n\nWhen that happens, failing the batch returns its buffer to the pool, and a new batch can immediately reuse that same buffer. Meanwhile, the client's poll continues writing the old batch's data from the now-corrupted buffer. The fix needs to prevent the buffer from being deallocated until the NetworkSend completes.\n\nI'm wondering if there's an even simpler ordering issue within `sendProducerData()` itself that I'm missing. I'm realizing the real issue: a batch that's been sitting in the accumulator long enough to exceed the delivery timeout would get drained, immediately marked as in-flight, then caught by the expiry check and failed before it ever gets sent. That means the buffer gets deallocated, but then `sendProduceRequests` tries to send batches that no longer have allocated buffers. B1's buffer now holds B2's data, so when the broker receives B1's request, it stores B2's records under topic A instead—that's the actual race condition. All of this happens within `sendProducerData()`, with the buffer deallocation occurring before the send, leaving a window where another thread can reuse that same buffer. The real fix is to either call `failBatch` after sending the requests, or filter out expired batches before they're included in the send operation.\n\nLooking at how `sendProducerData()` is structured... I see the issue now — when a batch sits in the accumulator long enough to exceed the delivery timeout, it gets marked as expired in the same iteration it's drained and added to inFlightBatches, which means it could still be sent before being failed. The `MemoryRecords.buffer()` method returns a duplicate of the original buffer, which shares the same backing array—so when `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` adds this buffer to its list, both the original and duplicate point to the same underlying data. Let me write the solution.\n\nKey facts:\n1. `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` at line 140: `addBuffer(((MemoryRecords) records).buffer())` — adds a `ByteBuffer.duplicate()` that shares the same backing array as the batch's original ByteBuffer.\n2. The `Send` object built by `SendBuilder` holds this duplicate ByteBuffer.\n3. When `client.poll()` writes this `Send` to the socket, it reads from the ByteBuffer. If the write spans multiple `poll()` calls (socket buffer full), the ByteBuffer is referenced across iterations.\n\n\n4. When a batch expires, `failBatch()` deallocates its ByteBuffer back to the pool, where a producer thread can immediately reuse it for a new batch on a different topic, corrupting the data the pending `Send` is still trying to transmit.\n5. The root cause is that `SendBuilder` holds a direct reference to the batch's buffer without copying it, while `failBatch()` returns that buffer to the pool prematurely—the fix is to copy the buffer in `SendBuilder` so each `Send` owns independent this.free.add(buffer)`\n6. **Buffer reused by new batch for different topic**: User thread calls `producer.send()` → `RecordAccumulator.append()` → `BufferPool.allocate()` → `free.pollFirst()` returns the just-cleared buffer; new records for topic B are written into it\n7. **Bug triggered by**: `SendBuilder.java` — `writeRecords(BaseRecords)` (line 138–143): only a `ByteBuffer.duplicate()` (not a copy) was stored into the `Send` object, so the `ByteBufferSend` shares the backing `byte[]` array with the batch's original `ByteBuffer`; when the backing array is overwritten by the new batch, the still-pending network write reads corrupted data\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java`\n- **Function**: `writeRecords(BaseRecords records)`\n- **Line**: ~140 (and ~143 for `UnalignedMemoryRecords`)\n- **Explanation**:\n\n  When serializing a `ProduceRequest` for network transmission, `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` calls `((MemoryRecords) records).buffer()` which returns `buffer.duplicate()` — a `ByteBuffer` that shares the **same backing `byte[]` array** as the `ProducerBatch`'s original `ByteBuffer`. This duplicate is added to the `Send` object's buffer list (as a `ByteBufferSend`) for zero-copy network writing.\n\n  The `Send` object is then queued via `selector.send(new NetworkSend(..., send))`. The actual write to the socket happens in `client.poll()`, and may span **multiple poll iterations** if the socket's send buffer is full (partial write). During those iterations, the `ByteBufferSend` still holds a reference to the duplicate that shares the original batch's backing array.\n\n  Independently, when the in-flight batch expires (delivery timeout) or the broker disconnects, `Sender.sendProducerData()` calls `failBatch()` → `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` → `accumulator.deallocate(batch)` → `BufferPool.deallocate(batch.buffer(), ...)`. `BufferPool.deallocate()` calls `buffer.clear()` and adds the original `ByteBuffer` back to the free list. A producer user thread can then allocate this `ByteBuffer` for a brand-new batch on a **different topic**, and starts writing that topic's records into the backing array.\n\n  When the Sender thread's next `client.poll()` resumes the partial write for the **original** request, the `ByteBufferSend` reads from its duplicate, which now reflects the **new topic's record data** in the shared backing array. The broker receives the new records under the **original request's topic/partition header** (e.g., topic A) because the topic name is in the already-serialized request header, not in the record payload. The CRC on the records passes because it covers only key/value/headers, not the topic name.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\nThe safest minimal fix is to make an independent copy of the `ByteBuffer` content in `SendBuilder.writeRecords()`, so the `Send` object owns its data and is unaffected by subsequent buffer pool operations on the original batch buffer.\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java\n@@ -136,10 +136,18 @@ public class SendBuilder implements Writable {\n      */\n     @Override\n     public void writeRecords(BaseRecords records) {\n         if (records instanceof MemoryRecords) {\n             flushPendingBuffer();\n-            addBuffer(((MemoryRecords) records).buffer());\n+            ByteBuffer src = ((MemoryRecords) records).buffer();\n+            ByteBuffer copy = ByteBuffer.allocate(src.remaining());\n+            copy.put(src);\n+            copy.flip();\n+            addBuffer(copy);\n         } else if (records instanceof UnalignedMemoryRecords) {\n             flushPendingBuffer();\n-            addBuffer(((UnalignedMemoryRecords) records).buffer());\n+            ByteBuffer src = ((UnalignedMemoryRecords) records).buffer();\n+            ByteBuffer copy = ByteBuffer.allocate(src.remaining());\n+            copy.put(src);\n+            copy.flip();\n+            addBuffer(copy);\n         } else {\n             flushPendingSend();\n             addSend(records.toSend());\n```\n\n**Alternative (more efficient) fix**: Defer `BufferPool.deallocate()` until the associated `NetworkSend` is confirmed complete. In `NetworkClient.handleCompletedSends()`, when a send is moved to `completedSends()`, the Sender could be notified to then release the batch buffer. This preserves the zero-copy property but requires plumbing a \"send-complete\" callback from `NetworkClient` back to `RecordAccumulator`/`Sender`. Specifically:\n\n- In `Sender.sendProduceRequest()`, after `client.send(clientRequest, now)`, register the batch buffers as \"pending release\".\n- In `Sender.handleProduceResponse()` (the `RequestCompletionHandler` callback), release the buffer after the send is confirmed either complete or cancelled due to disconnect.\n- `failBatch()` for expired in-flight batches should skip the `accumulator.deallocate()` call and defer it to the completion callback.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Step 1 — `sendProducerData()` ordering flaw (`Sender.java` lines 357–443)\n\n```java\n// Line 395: drain fresh batches\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(...);\n// Line 396: immediately mark them as in-flight\naddToInflightBatches(batches);\n\n// Lines 406-423: expire *all* in-flight batches (including ones just added above!)\n// and return their ByteBuffers to the pool via failBatch()\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n...\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n    failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(...), false); // ← deallocates buffer\n}\n\n// Line 442: THEN send — but some batches' backing buffers were just freed!\nsendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n```\n\nThis contains **two overlapping races**:\n\n**Race A (same iteration):** A batch that has lingered in the accumulator past `delivery.timeout.ms` is drained, immediately added to `inFlightBatches`, immediately expired by `getExpiredInflightBatches`, its buffer freed by `failBatch`, then its stale `MemoryRecords` (backed by the freed buffer) is included in `sendProduceRequests`. Between `failBatch` and `sendProduceRequests` another thread can write new records into that buffer.\n\n**Race B (cross-iteration):** A batch drained and sent in a previous `runOnce()` iteration may have only been **partially written** to the socket (socket buffer full — `ByteBufferSend.remaining() > 0`). The `NetworkSend` remains pending in the `Selector`. In the current iteration, `failBatch` frees that batch's buffer. A producer user thread immediately reallocates it for a new batch on a different topic. When `client.poll()` resumes the partial write, `ByteBufferSend` reads the new topic's data from the shared backing array and sends it under the old topic's request header.\n\n### Step 2 — `failBatch()` → `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` (`Sender.java` lines 825–836)\n\n```java\nif (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n    ...\n    maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // ← triggers premature deallocation\n}\n```\n\n`maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch` removes the batch from the in-flight tracker and calls `accumulator.deallocate(batch)`.\n\n### Step 3 — `RecordAccumulator.deallocate()` and `BufferPool.deallocate()` (`RecordAccumulator.java` line 1032; `BufferPool.java` lines 260–275)\n\n```java\n// RecordAccumulator.java\nfree.deallocate(batch.buffer(), batch.initialCapacity());\n\n// BufferPool.java\nif (size == this.poolableSize && size == buffer.capacity()) {\n    buffer.clear();          // resets position=0, limit=capacity; data unchanged but now writable\n    this.free.add(buffer);   // made available for re-allocation immediately\n}\n```\n\nAnother thread calling `BufferPool.allocate()` can receive this buffer and start writing new records into its backing array before the pending `Send` has finished reading from it.\n\n### Step 4 — `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` retains a shared reference (`SendBuilder.java` lines 137–147)\n\n```java\n@Override\npublic void writeRecords(BaseRecords records) {\n    if (records instanceof MemoryRecords) {\n        flushPendingBuffer();\n        addBuffer(((MemoryRecords) records).buffer());  // ← duplicate, NOT a copy\n    }\n    ...\n}\n```\n\n`MemoryRecords.buffer()` returns `buffer.duplicate()` — a new `ByteBuffer` object with independent position/limit/mark but the **same backing `byte[]` array**. `addBuffer()` stores this duplicate in the `ByteBufferSend`. Any write to the original buffer's backing array (by the new batch) is immediately visible through the duplicate, corrupting the pending send.\n\n### Why messages appear on the wrong topic\n\nThe Kafka ProduceRequest wire format separates the **request header** (topic name, partition index — serialized eagerly into a fresh byte array by `SendBuilder`) from the **record payload** (serialized as a reference to the `MemoryRecords` ByteBuffer). After `request.toSend(header)` returns, the topic name is safely encoded in an independent buffer. The record payload, however, is only a reference. When the backing array is overwritten with topic B's records, the broker receives:\n\n- Header: `topic = A, partition = 0`  ← correct, from the eagerly serialized header\n- Records: topic B's key/value/headers ← corrupted, from the reused buffer\n\nThe record-level CRC covers only the record attributes (key, value, headers, timestamp) — it does not cover the topic/partition in the request envelope. So the CRC passes, the broker appends the records to topic A's log, and consumers of topic A see messages that were intended for topic B.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":106,"cache_read_input_tokens":75012,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":106,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":18,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"326eb7ac-b8bf-41b9-891c-3382232b8412","uuid":"a1e049e5-623d-4ed9-b96c-fe2e170b9904"}

The record-level CRC passes because it covers only key/value/headers, not the topic name in the request envelope.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java\n@@ -136,10 +136,18 @@ public class SendBuilder implements Writable {\n      */\n     @Override\n     public void writeRecords(BaseRecords records) {\n         if (records instanceof MemoryRecords) {\n             flushPendingBuffer();\n-            addBuffer(((MemoryRecords) records).buffer());\n+            ByteBuffer src = ((MemoryRecords) records).buffer();\n+            ByteBuffer copy = ByteBuffer.allocate(src.remaining());\n+            copy.put(src);\n+            copy.flip();\n+            addBuffer(copy);\n         } else if (records instanceof UnalignedMemoryRecords) {\n             flushPendingBuffer();\n-            addBuffer(((UnalignedMemoryRecords) records).buffer());\n+            ByteBuffer src = ((UnalignedMemoryRecords) records).buffer();\n+            ByteBuffer copy = ByteBuffer.allocate(src.remaining());\n+            copy.put(src);\n+            copy.flip();\n+            addBuffer(copy);\n         } else {\n             flushPendingSend();\n             addSend(records.toSend());\n```\n\nThis ensures the `Send` object owns an independent copy of the record data, so reuse of the batch's `ByteBuffer` by `BufferPool` cannot affect the in-flight network write.\n\n**Alternative (zero-copy-preserving) fix**: Defer `BufferPool.deallocate()` for in-flight batches until the associated `NetworkSend` is confirmed fully written. In `Sender.sendProduceRequest()`, register each batch as \"buffer pending release\". The `RequestCompletionHandler` callback (`handleProduceResponse`) — which fires after the send is complete or the connection is dropped — then calls `accumulator.deallocate()`. `failBatch()` for expired in-flight batches should skip the `accumulator.deallocate()` call, leaving buffer cleanup to the completion callback. This preserves zero-copy semantics but requires plumbing a deferred-deallocation mechanism through `Sender` and `NetworkClient`.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Step 1 — `sendProducerData()` ordering creates the window (`Sender.java` lines 357-443)\n\n```java\n// Line 395: drain fresh batches\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(...);\n// Line 396: immediately mark them as in-flight\naddToInflightBatches(batches);\n\n// Lines 406-423: expire ALL in-flight batches (including ones just added above)\n// and return their ByteBuffers to the pool via failBatch()\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n...\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n    failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(...), false); // deallocates buffer NOW\n}\n\n// Line 442: THEN send — but some batches' backing buffers may be freed already\nsendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n// After this method returns, client.poll() runs, which may also resume a\n// partial write whose buffer was freed above.\n```\n\nThere are two overlapping races:\n\n**Race A (same iteration):** A batch lingering past `delivery.timeout.ms` in the accumulator is drained, added to `inFlightBatches`, immediately expired by `getExpiredInflightBatches`, its buffer freed by `failBatch`, then its stale `MemoryRecords` (backed by the freed buffer) is included in `sendProduceRequests`. Between `failBatch` and the network write another thread can overwrite that buffer with new records.\n\n**Race B (cross-iteration):** A batch drained and sent in a previous `runOnce()` may have been only **partially written** to the socket (socket buffer full — `ByteBufferSend.remaining() > 0`). Its `NetworkSend` remains pending in the `Selector`. In the current iteration, `failBatch` frees that batch's buffer. A producer user thread reallocates it for a new batch on a different topic. When `client.poll()` resumes the partial write, `ByteBufferSend` reads the new topic's data from the shared backing array and sends it under the old topic's request header.\n\n### Step 2 — `failBatch()` triggers premature deallocation (`Sender.java` lines ~825-836)\n\n```java\nif (batch.completeExceptionally(topLevelException, recordExceptions)) {\n    ...\n    maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch(batch);  // triggers premature pool return\n}\n```\n\n### Step 3 — `BufferPool.deallocate()` immediately makes the buffer available (`BufferPool.java` lines ~263-265)\n\n```java\nbuffer.clear();          // resets position/limit; data unchanged but buffer is now \"empty\"\nthis.free.add(buffer);   // immediately available for re-allocation\n```\n\nA concurrent `BufferPool.allocate()` call on the user thread receives this buffer and starts writing new records into the shared backing array before the pending `Send` finishes reading it.\n\n### Step 4 — `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` stores only a duplicate, not a copy (`SendBuilder.java` lines ~138-147)\n\n```java\naddBuffer(((MemoryRecords) records).buffer());  // duplicate shares backing byte[]\n```\n\n`MemoryRecords.buffer()` returns `buffer.duplicate()`: same backing `byte[]`, independent position/limit/mark. The `ByteBufferSend` reads from this duplicate during network writes. Any write to the original buffer's backing array (by the new batch) is immediately visible through the duplicate, corrupting the pending send.\n\n### Why messages appear on the wrong topic\n\nThe Kafka ProduceRequest wire format separates the **request header** (topic name, partition index — serialized eagerly into a fresh heap buffer by `SendBuilder` for the fixed-size fields) from the **record payload** (serialized as a zero-copy reference to the `MemoryRecords` backing buffer). After `request.toSend(header)` returns, the topic name is safely encoded in an independent buffer. The record payload is only a reference.\n\nWhen the backing array is overwritten with topic B's records, the broker receives:\n- Header: `topic = A, partition = 0`  (correct — from the eagerly serialized header)\n- Records: topic B's key/value/headers  (corrupted — from the reused buffer)\n\nThe record-level CRC covers only record attributes (key, value, headers, timestamp) — not the topic/partition in the request envelope — so the CRC passes, the broker appends topic B's records to topic A's log, and consumers of topic A see messages intended for topic B.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":374,"cache_read_input_tokens":78564,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":374,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"326eb7ac-b8bf-41b9-891c-3382232b8412","uuid":"999a5171-a4a6-4fa5-af8f-03f90c097e58"}

when the backing array is overwritten by the new batch, the still-pending network write reads corrupted data\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java`\n- **Function**: `writeRecords(BaseRecords records)`\n- **Line**: ~140 (and ~143 for `UnalignedMemoryRecords`)\n- **Explanation**:\n\n  When serializing a `ProduceRequest` for network transmission, `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` calls `((MemoryRecords) records).buffer()` which returns `buffer.duplicate()` — a `ByteBuffer` that shares the **same backing `byte[]` array** as the `ProducerBatch`'s original `ByteBuffer`. This duplicate is added to the `Send` object's buffer list (becoming part of a `ByteBufferSend`) for zero-copy network writing.\n\n  The `Send` object is then queued via `selector.send(new NetworkSend(..., send))`. The actual write to the socket happens in `client.poll()` and may span **multiple poll iterations** if the socket's send buffer is full (partial write). During those iterations, the `ByteBufferSend` still holds a live reference to the duplicate, which shares the original batch's backing array.\n\n  Independently, when the in-flight batch expires (delivery timeout) or its broker disconnects, `Sender.sendProducerData()` calls `failBatch()` -> `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` -> `accumulator.deallocate(batch)` -> `BufferPool.deallocate(batch.buffer(), ...)`. `BufferPool.deallocate()` calls `buffer.clear()` and adds the original `ByteBuffer` back to the free list. A producer user thread can then allocate this `ByteBuffer` for a brand-new batch on a **different topic** and start writing that topic's records into the shared backing array.\n\n  When the Sender thread's next `client.poll()` resumes the partial write, `ByteBufferSend` reads from its duplicate, which now reflects the **new topic's record data** in the shared backing array. The broker receives the new records under the **original request's topic/partition header** (e.g., topic A) because the topic name is in the already-serialized request header, not the record payload. The record-level CRC passes because it covers only key/value/headers, not the topic name in the request envelope.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n```diff\n--- a/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java\n+++ b/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/protocol/SendBuilder.java\n@@ -136,10 +136,18 @@ public class SendBuilder implements Writable {\n      */\n     @Override\n     public void writeRecords(BaseRecords records) {\n         if (records instanceof MemoryRecords) {\n             flushPendingBuffer();\n-            addBuffer(((MemoryRecords) records).buffer());\n+            ByteBuffer src = ((MemoryRecords) records).buffer();\n+            ByteBuffer copy = ByteBuffer.allocate(src.remaining());\n+            copy.put(src);\n+            copy.flip();\n+            addBuffer(copy);\n         } else if (records instanceof UnalignedMemoryRecords) {\n             flushPendingBuffer();\n-            addBuffer(((UnalignedMemoryRecords) records).buffer());\n+            ByteBuffer src = ((UnalignedMemoryRecords) records).buffer();\n+            ByteBuffer copy = ByteBuffer.allocate(src.remaining());\n+            copy.put(src);\n+            copy.flip();\n+            addBuffer(copy);\n         } else {\n             flushPendingSend();\n             addSend(records.toSend());\n```\n\nThis ensures the `Send` object owns an independent copy of the record data, so reuse of the batch's `ByteBuffer` by `BufferPool` cannot affect the in-flight network write.\n\n**Alternative (zero-copy-preserving) fix**: Defer `BufferPool.deallocate()` for in-flight batches until the associated `NetworkSend` is confirmed fully written. In `Sender.sendProduceRequest()`, register each batch as \"buffer pending release\". The `RequestCompletionHandler` callback (`handleProduceResponse`) — which fires after the send is complete or the connection is dropped — then calls `accumulator.deallocate()`. `failBatch()` for expired in-flight batches should skip the `accumulator.deallocate()` call, leaving buffer cleanup to the completion callback. This preserves zero-copy semantics but requires plumbing a deferred-deallocation mechanism through `Sender` and `NetworkClient`.\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Step 1 — `sendProducerData()` ordering creates the window (`Sender.java` lines 357-443)\n\n```java\n// Line 395: drain fresh batches\nMap<Integer, List<ProducerBatch>> batches = this.accumulator.drain(...);\n// Line 396: immediately mark them as in-flight\naddToInflightBatches(batches);\n\n// Lines 406-423: expire ALL in-flight batches (including ones just added above)\n// and return their ByteBuffers to the pool via failBatch()\nList<ProducerBatch> expiredInflightBatches = getExpiredInflightBatches(now);\n...\nfor (ProducerBatch expiredBatch : expiredBatches) {\n    failBatch(expiredBatch, new TimeoutException(...), false); // deallocates buffer NOW\n}\n\n// Line 442: THEN send — but some batches' backing buffers may be freed already\nsendProduceRequests(batches, now);\n// After this method returns, client.poll() runs, which may also resume a\n// partial write whose buffer was freed above.\n```\n\nThere are two overlapping races:\n\n**Race A (same iteration):** A batch lingering past `delivery.timeout.ms` in the accumulator is drained, added to `inFlightBatches`, immediately expired by `getExpiredInflightBatches`, its buffer freed by `failBatch`, then its stale `MemoryRecords` (backed by the freed buffer) is included in `sendProduceRequests`. This duplicate is retained inside the `Send` object queued for network writing.\n\n### How the Race Unfolds\n\n1. **Batch B1** (topic A) is serialized for network transmission. `SendBuilder.writeRecords()` stores a duplicate of B1's `ByteBuffer` in the `ByteBufferSend`. The `NetworkSend` is queued in the `Selector`.\n\n2. **Partial write**: `client.poll()` writes part of B1's data to the socket, but the socket buffer is full — `ByteBufferSend` still has bytes remaining. The `NetworkSend` stays pending across iterations.\n\n3. **Expiry**: In the next `sendProducerData()` call, `getExpiredInflightBatches()` finds B1 timed out. `failBatch()` → `maybeRemoveAndDeallocateBatch()` → `BufferPool.deallocate(B1.buffer)`: `buffer.clear()` and `free.add(buffer)` — **B1's buffer is returned to the pool while the NetworkSend is still pending**.\n\n4. **Reuse**: A producer user thread allocates B1's buffer for a new **batch B2 on topic B**, writing topic B's records into the shared backing array.\n\n5. **Corruption**: `client.poll()` resumes the partial write for B1's `NetworkSend`. The `ByteBufferSend` reads from its duplicate, which shares B1's now-overwritten backing array. The socket receives topic B's records, but the already-serialized request header says \"topic A, partition 0\". The broker stores topic B's records in topic A. Buffer pool reuse can no longer affect in-flight writes.
